214:
215:function isNonRetryableError(err: unknown): boolean {
216:  const e = err as { statusCode?: number; code?: string; message?: string };
217:  if (e.statusCode === 400 || e.statusCode === 401 || e.statusCode === 403) return true;
218:  if (e.code === 'PROVIDER_NOT_CONFIGURED') return true;
219:  // Rev §6 — caller-initiated aborts must not retry. The caller decided to
220:  // stop; re-hitting the provider on their behalf wastes tokens and can
221:  // produce confusing duplicate calls in the Anthropic console.
222:  if (e.code === 'CLIENT_DISCONNECTED') return true;
223:  // Provider timeouts are "ambiguous state" — the provider may have already
224:  // completed generation server-side. A retry under the same idempotency key
225:  // would issue a second concurrent call and double-bill at the provider
226:  // layer (no LLM provider currently supports request-level dedup headers).
227:  // Propagate immediately; the caller decides whether to replay under a new
228:  // idempotency key. See spec §17 deferred items.
229:  if (e.code === 'PROVIDER_TIMEOUT') return true;
230:  const code = (e.code ?? '').toLowerCase();
231:  return code.includes('auth') || code.includes('invalid') || code.includes('bad_request');
232:}

234:// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
235:// IEE run-id resolver (Hermes Tier 1 Phase C §7.6)
236:// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
237://
238:// The cost breaker requires an `agent_runs.id` (`runId`) to look up the
239:// per-run cost ceiling. IEE-sourced calls (`sourceType='iee'`) may or may
240:// not carry `runId` directly; when they don't, `ieeRunId` is the handle
241:// and the parent `agent_run_id` lives on `iee_runs`.
242://
243:// Kept local to the router per §7.6: the breaker stays agnostic about how
244:// its `runId` was derived, and the router already owns `iee_runs` reads
245:// for other routing metadata. One indexed primary-key lookup per
246:// `routeCall`; no memoisation across calls (the cache key would be
247:// `routeCall` invocation itself, and each invocation runs once).
248:async function resolveRunIdFromIee(ieeRunId: string | undefined): Promise<string | null> {
249:  if (!ieeRunId) return null;
250:  const [row] = await db
251:    .select({ agentRunId: ieeRuns.agentRunId })
252:    .from(ieeRuns)
253:    .where(eq(ieeRuns.id, ieeRunId))
254:    .limit(1);
255:  return row?.agentRunId ?? null;
256:}

258:// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
259:// Main router — drop-in replacement for callAnthropic()
260:// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
261:
262:export async function routeCall(params: RouterCallParams): Promise<ProviderResponse> {
263:  const routerStart = Date.now();
264:  // `queuedAt` — captured at the very top of routeCall so the gap between
265:  // caller invocation and adapter dispatch (budget lock wait, provider
266:  // cooldown bounce chain, model resolver) is visible to the In-Flight tab.
267:  // See deferred-items brief §3. Pre-dispatch terminals (budget_blocked,
268:  // rate_limited) never produce a registry entry so `queuedAt` only surfaces
269:  // on entries that reach inflightRegistry.add().
270:  const queuedAt = new Date(routerStart).toISOString();
271:
272:  // ── 1. Validate context ─────────────────────────────────────────────────
273:  const ctx = LLMCallContextSchema.parse(params.context);
274:
275:  // ── 1a. IEE contract guards (rev 6 §13.1) ───────────────────────────────
276:  // Two layers protect cost-attribution integrity for IEE runs:
277:  //   1. This runtime guard — fast feedback to the caller.
278:  //   2. A database CHECK constraint (llm_requests_iee_requires_run_id) that
279:  //      catches any future code path that bypasses the router.
280:  if (ctx.sourceType === 'iee' && !ctx.ieeRunId) {
281:    throw new RouterContractError('llmRouter: ieeRunId is required when sourceType="iee"');
282:  }
283:  if (ctx.callSite === 'worker' && !ctx.ieeRunId) {
284:    throw new RouterContractError('llmRouter: ieeRunId is required when callSite="worker"');
285:  }
286:
287:  // ── 1a'. Rev §6 — polymorphic attribution + feature-tag guards ───────────
288:  //
289:  // Mirrors the DB CHECK constraint llm_requests_attribution_ck from
290:  // migration 0185. Fails closed at the router so callers get an immediate
291:  // contract error rather than a cryptic 23514 from Postgres.
292:  if (ctx.sourceType === 'analyzer') {
293:    if (!ctx.sourceId) {
294:      throw new RouterContractError('llmRouter: sourceId is required when sourceType="analyzer"');
295:    }
296:    if (ctx.runId || ctx.executionId || ctx.ieeRunId) {
297:      throw new RouterContractError(
298:        'llmRouter: analyzer rows must not set runId/executionId/ieeRunId — use sourceId instead',
299:      );
300:    }
301:  }
302:  if (ctx.sourceType === 'agent_run' && !ctx.runId) {
303:    throw new RouterContractError('llmRouter: runId is required when sourceType="agent_run"');
304:  }
305:  if (ctx.sourceType === 'process_execution' && !ctx.executionId) {
306:    throw new RouterContractError('llmRouter: executionId is required when sourceType="process_execution"');
307:  }
308:  // executionPhase must be set for billable (agent-execution) rows and NULL
309:  // for system/analyzer — mirrors DB CHECK llm_requests_execution_phase_ck.
310:  const isSystemScoped = ctx.sourceType === 'system' || ctx.sourceType === 'analyzer';
311:  if (!isSystemScoped && !ctx.executionPhase) {
312:    throw new RouterContractError(
313:      `llmRouter: executionPhase is required when sourceType="${ctx.sourceType}"`,
314:    );
315:  }
316:  if (isSystemScoped && ctx.executionPhase) {
317:    throw new RouterContractError(
318:      `llmRouter: executionPhase must be null when sourceType="${ctx.sourceType}"`,
319:    );
320:  }
321:  // Feature-tag hygiene — warn (don't throw) when a caller forgets to tag.
322:  // In tests, the default 'unknown' is expected; in production code paths
323:  // it signals a missed wiring opportunity for the System P&L page.
324:  if (!ctx.featureTag && process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'test') {
325:    console.warn('[llmRouter] missing feature_tag', {
326:      sourceType: ctx.sourceType,
327:      organisationId: ctx.organisationId,
328:    });
329:  }
330:
331:  // ── 1b. Resolve provider + model from execution phase ─────────────────
332:  let effectiveProvider: string;
333:  let effectiveModel: string;
334:  let routingTier: 'frontier' | 'economy' = 'frontier';
335:  let wasDowngraded = false;
336:  let routingReason: string = 'ceiling';
337:
338:  const systemCallerPolicy = ctx.systemCallerPolicy ?? 'respect_routing';
339:  if (systemCallerPolicy === 'bypass_routing') {
340:    // Rev §6 — caller has pinned provider+model (typical for non-agent
341:    // consumers whose prompts are model-specific). Skip resolveLLM() but
342:    // still go through the router so the call lands in llm_requests.
343:    effectiveProvider = ctx.provider ?? 'anthropic';
344:    effectiveModel = ctx.model ?? 'claude-sonnet-4-6';
345:    routingReason = 'forced';
346:  } else if (env.ROUTER_FORCE_FRONTIER) {
347:    // Kill switch: skip all routing, use ceiling model.
348:    effectiveProvider = ctx.provider ?? 'anthropic';
349:    effectiveModel = ctx.model ?? 'claude-sonnet-4-6';
350:    routingReason = 'forced';
351:  } else {
352:    // Fall through to the resolver. resolveLLM requires a concrete phase;
353:    // system-scoped callers should always use bypass_routing so this branch
354:    // is never reached without an executionPhase. If a caller misconfigures
355:    // themselves, fall back to 'execution' rather than throwing — the
356:    // runtime guard above already rejects the inconsistent combination.
357:    const resolved = resolveLLM({
358:      phase:    ctx.executionPhase ?? 'execution',
359:      taskType: ctx.taskType,
360:      ceiling:  (ctx.provider && ctx.model) ? { provider: ctx.provider, model: ctx.model } : undefined,
361:      mode:     ctx.routingMode ?? 'ceiling',
362:      constraints: {
363:        requiresToolCalling: !!(params.tools && params.tools.length > 0),
364:        estimatedContextTokens: params.estimatedContextTokens,
365:        expectedMaxOutputTokens: params.maxTokens,
366:      },
367:    });
368:
369:    if (env.ROUTER_SHADOW_MODE) {
370:      // Shadow mode: log what would have been used, but use ceiling
371:      console.info('[llmRouter] shadow:', JSON.stringify({
372:        wouldUse: { provider: resolved.provider, model: resolved.model, tier: resolved.tier },
373:        actuallyUsing: { provider: ctx.provider, model: ctx.model },
374:        reason: resolved.reason,
375:      }));
376:      effectiveProvider = ctx.provider ?? 'anthropic';
377:      effectiveModel = ctx.model ?? 'claude-sonnet-4-6';
378:      routingReason = 'ceiling';
379:    } else {
380:      effectiveProvider = resolved.provider;
381:      effectiveModel = resolved.model;
382:      routingTier = resolved.tier;
383:      wasDowngraded = resolved.wasDowngraded;
384:      routingReason = resolved.reason;
385:    }
386:  }
387:
388:  // ── 2. Check provider is registered ────────────────────────────────────
389:  const adapter = getProviderAdapter(effectiveProvider);
390:
391:  // ── 3. Generate idempotency key ─────────────────────────────────────────
392:  const idempotencyKey = generateIdempotencyKey(ctx, params.messages, effectiveProvider, effectiveModel);
393:
394:  // ── 4–7. Idempotency check + budget reservation (atomic transaction) ────
395:  // Wrap the idempotency lookup and budget reservation in a single transaction
396:  // so two concurrent requests with the same key cannot both pass through.
397:  const { billingMonth, billingDay } = getBillingPeriods();
398:
399:  // ── 5. Resolve pricing and estimate cost (outside tx — read-only, no race) ──
400:  const [pricing, margin] = await Promise.all([
401:    pricingService.getPricing(effectiveProvider, effectiveModel),
402:    pricingService.getMargin(ctx.organisationId),
403:  ]);
404:
405:  const maxTokensForEstimate = params.maxTokens ?? 4096;
406:  const estimatedCostCents = await pricingService.estimateCost(
407:    effectiveProvider, effectiveModel, maxTokensForEstimate, ctx.organisationId,
408:  );
409:
410:  // ── 6. Compute request payload hash ────────────────────────────────────
411:  const requestPayloadHash = createHash('sha256')
412:    .update(JSON.stringify(params.messages))
413:    .digest('hex');
414:
415:  // ── 4+7. Atomic idempotency check + provisional ledger write ───────────
416:  //
417:  // Deferred-items brief §1 — the provisional `'started'` row MUST be
418:  // inserted inside this transaction, not after. A SELECT FOR UPDATE only
419:  // locks existing rows; when no row exists for `idempotencyKey`, two
420:  // concurrent first-calls both pass the check, both commit, and both
421:  // proceed to dispatch — the exact double-bill window §1 exists to
422:  // prevent. Pulling the INSERT into the transaction makes the second
423:  // caller block on the unique-constraint conflict until the first
424:  // transaction commits; the second tx's own SELECT FOR UPDATE then
425:  // returns the `'started'` row and correctly takes the reconciliation
426:  // branch.
427:  //
428:  // pr-review finding #1 (2026-04-21): this contract was previously
429:  // violated — the INSERT was after the transaction and the race window
430:  // was open. DO NOT move the INSERT back out of this block.
431:  let reservationId: string | null = null;
432:  let budgetBlockedStatus: string | null = null;
433:  let budgetErrorMessage: string | null = null;
434:
435:  const idempotencyResult = await db.transaction(async (tx) => {
436:    // Check for existing record inside the transaction
437:    const existing = await tx
438:      .select()
439:      .from(llmRequests)
440:      .where(eq(llmRequests.idempotencyKey, idempotencyKey))
441:      .for('update')
442:      .limit(1);
443:
444:    if (existing.length > 0 && existing[0].status === 'success') {
445:      return {
446:        cached: true as const,
447:        response: {
448:          content:           '',
449:          stopReason:        'cached' as const,
450:          tokensIn:          existing[0].tokensIn,
451:          tokensOut:         existing[0].tokensOut,
452:          providerRequestId: existing[0].providerRequestId ?? '',
453:        },
454:      };
455:    }
456:
457:    // Deferred-items brief §1 — a provisional `'started'` row means a prior
458:    // attempt under the same idempotencyKey already called the provider
459:    // (which has billed). A retry cannot safely re-dispatch. Surface a
460:    // typed error so the caller owns the reconciliation decision.
461:    //
462:    // Important: this check is ONLY for rows whose status is literally
463:    // 'started'. Terminal error/timeout rows are still overwritable by
464:    // the usual upsert path (see `where status != 'success'` clause on
465:    // the success-insert at the bottom of this function).
466:    if (existing.length > 0 && existing[0].status === 'started') {
467:      return { inflight: true as const } as const;
468:    }
469:
470:    // Terminal error/terminal-failure rows from a prior attempt exist but
471:    // are overwritable — fall through to write a fresh `'started'` row
472:    // below. The upsert conflict target is idempotencyKey and the
473:    // onConflictDoUpdate `where: status != 'success'` guard keeps any
474:    // prior success row (which was already returned above) untouched.
475:    const provisional = await tx
476:      .insert(llmRequests)
477:      .values({
478:        idempotencyKey,
479:        organisationId:      ctx.organisationId,
480:        subaccountId:        ctx.subaccountId,
481:        userId:              ctx.userId,
482:        sourceType:          ctx.sourceType,
483:        runId:               ctx.runId,
484:        executionId:         ctx.executionId,
485:        ieeRunId:            ctx.ieeRunId,
486:        sourceId:            ctx.sourceId,
487:        featureTag:          ctx.featureTag ?? 'unknown',
488:        callSite:            ctx.callSite ?? 'app',
489:        agentName:           ctx.agentName,
490:        taskType:            ctx.taskType,
491:        executionPhase:      ctx.executionPhase,
492:        provider:            effectiveProvider,
493:        model:               effectiveModel,
494:        tokensIn:            0,
495:        tokensOut:           0,
496:        costRaw:             '0',
497:        costWithMargin:      '0',
498:        costWithMarginCents: 0,
499:        marginMultiplier:    String(margin.multiplier),
500:        fixedFeeCents:       margin.fixedFeeCents,
501:        requestPayloadHash,
502:        status:              'started',
503:        requestedProvider:   effectiveProvider,
504:        requestedModel:      effectiveModel,
505:        wasEscalated:        ctx.wasEscalated ?? false,
506:        escalationReason:    ctx.escalationReason,
507:        billingMonth,
508:        billingDay,
509:      })
510:      // A prior terminal-error row may still own this key. Overwrite it
511:      // with a fresh `'started'` so the retry path works as expected; the
512:      // `where: status != 'success'` guard protects committed successes
513:      // (which have already been caught and returned above anyway).
514:      //
515:      // `createdAt: sql\`now()\`` resets the row's age so a revived
516:      // terminal-error row (which may be hours old) doesn't appear
517:      // immediately sweep-eligible to `llmStartedRowSweepJob`. Without
518:      // this reset, a retry on a key whose prior error row is older than
519:      // PROVIDER_CALL_TIMEOUT_MS + 60s would be reaped by the sweep while
520:      // the provider call is still in flight — reopening the double-bill
521:      // window this provisional-row mechanism exists to prevent.
522:      .onConflictDoUpdate({
523:        target: [llmRequests.idempotencyKey],
524:        set: {
525:          status:              'started',
526:          errorMessage:        null,
527:          provider:            effectiveProvider,
528:          model:               effectiveModel,
529:          requestPayloadHash,
530:          requestedProvider:   effectiveProvider,
531:          requestedModel:      effectiveModel,
532:          marginMultiplier:    String(margin.multiplier),
533:          fixedFeeCents:       margin.fixedFeeCents,
534:          tokensIn:            0,
535:          tokensOut:           0,
536:          costRaw:             '0',
537:          costWithMargin:      '0',
538:          costWithMarginCents: 0,
539:          createdAt:           sql`now()`,
540:        },
541:        where: sql`${llmRequests.status} != 'success'`,
542:      })
543:      .returning({ id: llmRequests.id });
544:
545:    return { cached: false as const, provisionalRowId: provisional[0]?.id ?? null };
546:  });
547:
548:  if ('inflight' in idempotencyResult) {
549:    createEvent('llm.router.reconciliation_required', {
550:      idempotencyKey,
551:      model: effectiveModel,
552:      provider: effectiveProvider,
553:    });
554:    throw new ReconciliationRequiredError({ idempotencyKey });
555:  }
556:
557:  if (idempotencyResult.cached) {
558:    createEvent('llm.router.cache_hit', {
559:      idempotencyKey,
560:      model: effectiveModel,
561:      provider: effectiveProvider,
562:    });
563:    return idempotencyResult.response;
564:  }
565:  // `idempotencyResult.provisionalRowId` is populated at this point but
566:  // isn't threaded downstream — the terminal upsert at the bottom of
567:  // routeCall uses the idempotencyKey as the conflict target, not the
568:  // row id. Kept on the return shape for future debugging / breaker
569:  // wiring without re-opening the concurrency window.
570:
571:  try {
572:    reservationId = await budgetService.checkAndReserve(
573:      {
574:        organisationId:    ctx.organisationId,
575:        subaccountId:      ctx.subaccountId,
576:        runId:             ctx.runId,
577:        subaccountAgentId: ctx.subaccountAgentId,
578:        sourceType:        ctx.sourceType,
579:        billingDay,
580:        billingMonth,
581:      },
582:      estimatedCostCents,
583:      idempotencyKey,
584:    );
585:  } catch (err) {
586:    if (err instanceof BudgetExceededError) {
587:      budgetBlockedStatus = 'budget_blocked';
588:      budgetErrorMessage = err.message;
589:      createEvent('llm.router.budget_exceeded', {
590:        estimatedCostCents,
591:        reason: 'insufficient_budget',
592:      });
593:    } else if (err instanceof RateLimitError) {
594:      budgetBlockedStatus = 'rate_limited';
595:      budgetErrorMessage = err.message;
596:    } else {
597:      throw err;
598:    }
599:  }
600:
601:  // Write the audit record for blocked calls (budget_blocked / rate_limited).
602:  // The provisional `'started'` row was already inserted inside the
603:  // idempotency-check transaction above, so we must overwrite it here
604:  // — not onConflictDoNothing — otherwise the `'started'` row stays in
605:  // the table until the sweep reaps it 660s later. `where status != 'success'`
606:  // preserves the invariant that a committed success is never downgraded.
607:  if (budgetBlockedStatus) {
608:    const budgetBlockedInsertedRows = await db
609:      .insert(llmRequests)
610:      .values({
611:        idempotencyKey,
612:        organisationId:      ctx.organisationId,
613:        subaccountId:        ctx.subaccountId,
614:        userId:              ctx.userId,
615:        sourceType:          ctx.sourceType,
616:        runId:               ctx.runId,
617:        executionId:         ctx.executionId,
618:        ieeRunId:            ctx.ieeRunId,        // §11.7.1
619:        sourceId:            ctx.sourceId,        // rev §6
620:        featureTag:          ctx.featureTag ?? 'unknown',  // rev §6
621:        callSite:            ctx.callSite ?? 'app',
622:        agentName:           ctx.agentName,
623:        taskType:            ctx.taskType,
624:        executionPhase:      ctx.executionPhase,  // nullable for system/analyzer
625:        provider:            effectiveProvider,
626:        model:               effectiveModel,
627:        tokensIn:            0,
628:        tokensOut:           0,
629:        costRaw:             '0',
630:        costWithMargin:      '0',
631:        costWithMarginCents: 0,
632:        marginMultiplier:    String(margin.multiplier),
633:        fixedFeeCents:       margin.fixedFeeCents,
634:        requestPayloadHash,
635:        routerOverheadMs:    Date.now() - routerStart,
636:        status:              budgetBlockedStatus,
637:        errorMessage:        budgetErrorMessage,
638:        requestedProvider:   effectiveProvider,
639:        requestedModel:      effectiveModel,
640:        wasEscalated:        ctx.wasEscalated ?? false,
641:        escalationReason:    ctx.escalationReason,
642:        billingMonth,
643:        billingDay,
644:      })
645:      .onConflictDoUpdate({
646:        target: [llmRequests.idempotencyKey],
647:        set: {
648:          status:           budgetBlockedStatus,
649:          errorMessage:     budgetErrorMessage,
650:          routerOverheadMs: Date.now() - routerStart,
651:        },
652:        // Dual-review round 2 / reviewer feedback: tighten from
653:        // `!= 'success'` to `= 'started'`. The budget-blocked path runs
654:        // milliseconds after the provisional INSERT in the idempotency tx,
655:        // so the row is expected to be in 'started' state. A mismatch
656:        // (sweep fired, prior retry already terminalised, etc.) means
657:        // something raced and the budget-block's audit record is being
658:        // silently discarded — log it rather than swallow.
659:        where: sql`${llmRequests.status} = 'started'`,
660:      })
661:      .returning({ id: llmRequests.id });
662:
663:    if (budgetBlockedInsertedRows.length === 0) {
664:      logger.warn('llm_router.budget_block_upsert_ghost', {
665:        idempotencyKey,
666:        budgetBlockedStatus,
667:        note: 'existing row was not in started state — audit trail dropped',
668:      });
669:    }
670:
671:    throw {
672:      statusCode: 402,
673:      code: budgetBlockedStatus === 'budget_blocked' ? 'BUDGET_EXCEEDED' : 'RATE_LIMITED',
674:      message: budgetErrorMessage,
675:    };
676:  }
677:
678:  // ── 8. Call the provider with retry-fallback loop ───────────────────────
679:  // (The provisional `'started'` row is now written atomically inside the
680:  // idempotency-check transaction above — see the brief §1 / pr-review
681:  // finding #1. Do NOT re-introduce a separate post-transaction INSERT.)
682:  const providerStart = Date.now();
683:  let providerResponse: ProviderResponse | null = null;
684:  let callStatus: string = 'success';
685:  let callError: string | null = null;
686:  let attemptNumber = 1;
687:  let actualProvider = effectiveProvider;
688:  let actualModel = effectiveModel;
689:  const fallbackAttempts: FallbackAttempt[] = [];
690:
691:  // ── In-flight registry wiring (spec tasks/llm-inflight-realtime-tracker-spec.md) ──
692:  //
693:  // `currentRuntimeKey` tracks the attempt currently represented in the
694:  // in-flight registry. It is set immediately before each provider
695:  // dispatch and cleared after `inflightRegistry.remove()`. The final
696:  // attempt's removal fires AFTER the ledger upsert so the removal event
697:  // carries `ledgerRowId` + `ledgerCommittedAt` for UI reconciliation.
698:  //
699:  // An unhandled throw between add() and remove() (e.g. a DB error during
700:  // the ledger upsert) leaves the entry alive until the deadline-based
701:  // sweep reaps it — the 30s buffer past `timeoutMs` captures exactly that
702:  // window. See `llmInflightRegistry.ts` sweep loop for the safety net.
703:  let currentRuntimeKey: string | null = null;
704:  // When every attempt is a retryable error, each inner-catch removal
705:  // clears `currentRuntimeKey` before the outer failure-path ledger
706:  // write fires — which means the final failure's ledger row never gets
707:  // linked into the registry's removal event. We record the final
708:  // removed attempt here so the failure path can call
709:  // `inflightRegistry.updateLedgerLink()` with the now-known row id,
710:  // closing the UX gap flagged in pr-review — "[ledger] button missing
711:  // for retryable-error-only failures".
712:  let lastRemovedAttempt: {
713:    runtimeKey:     string;
714:    idempotencyKey: string;
715:    attempt:        number;
716:    startedAt:      string;
717:    terminalStatus: 'error';
718:  } | null = null;
719:
720:  // Cross-provider monotonic counter — ticks once per attempt whether the
721:  // attempt succeeds, retries, or fans out to a fallback provider. Paired
722:  // with the per-provider `attempt` counter so the In-Flight tab can show
723:  // "#3 of the logical call" instead of misleadingly showing "#1 (again)"
724:  // whenever the fallback chain advances. See deferred-items brief §4.
725:  let attemptSequence = 0;
726:
727:  // Build fallback chain: primary provider first, then others in order
728:  const fallbackChain = [
729:    effectiveProvider,
730:    ...PROVIDER_FALLBACK_CHAIN.filter(p => p !== effectiveProvider),
731:  ];
732:
733:  let lastError: unknown = null;
734:  let fallbackIndex = -1;
735:
736:  providerLoop:
737:  for (const provider of fallbackChain) {
738:    fallbackIndex++;
739:    if (isProviderCoolingDown(provider)) {
740:      console.warn(`[llmRouter] Skipping provider ${provider} — in cooldown`);
741:      continue;
742:    }
743:
744:    // Map the original model to the equivalent model for this provider
745:    const mappedModel = provider === effectiveProvider
746:      ? effectiveModel
747:      : FALLBACK_MODEL_MAP[provider]?.[effectiveModel];
748:
749:    // Skip this fallback provider if there is no explicit model mapping for it
750:    if (mappedModel === undefined) {
751:      console.warn(`[llmRouter] No model mapping for ${provider}/${ctx.model} — skipping`);
752:      continue;
753:    }
754:
755:    let providerAdapter;
756:    try {
757:      providerAdapter = getProviderAdapter(provider);
758:    } catch {
759:      // Provider not registered — skip
760:      continue;
761:    }
762:
763:    for (let attempt = 1; attempt <= PROVIDER_MAX_RETRIES + 1; attempt++) {
764:      // In-flight registry — one entry per attempt. runtimeKey is unique
765:      // across crash-restarts (see spec §4.2). add() fires post-budget-
766:      // reservation, immediately before the adapter dispatch.
767:      //
768:      // NOTE — `attempt` is the per-provider retry counter; it resets to
769:      // 1 on each fallback provider. The ledger's `attemptNumber` resets
770:      // the same way (line `attemptNumber = attempt` below), so the two
771:      // stay consistent, but the admin UI sees provider-B-attempt-1
772:      // immediately after provider-A-attempt-2 with no visible indication
773:      // that the earlier provider already failed. Distinct runtimeKeys
774:      // (different startedAt) prevent collision; the UX gap is a
775:      // documented follow-up, not a correctness bug.
776:      const attemptStartedAt = new Date().toISOString();
777:      const attemptRuntimeKey = buildRuntimeKey({
778:        idempotencyKey,
779:        attempt,
780:        startedAt: attemptStartedAt,
781:      });
782:      // Pre-add invariant (spec §6 llmRouter.ts row). Fail fast in dev so
783:      // an accidental double-add from a future refactor is caught at the
784:      // call site rather than silently becoming a registry-layer no-op.
785:      if (inflightRegistry.has(attemptRuntimeKey)) {
786:        const invariantMsg =
787:          `[llmRouter] inflight double-add invariant violated runtimeKey=${attemptRuntimeKey}`;
788:        if (process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production') {
789:          throw new Error(invariantMsg);
790:        }
791:        console.error(invariantMsg);
792:      }
793:      // Tick the cross-provider sequence immediately before add() so the
794:      // registry entry carries the correct "this is the Nth attempt of
795:      // the logical call" value regardless of which provider is running.
796:      attemptSequence++;
797:      inflightRegistry.add({
798:        idempotencyKey,
799:        attempt,
800:        attemptSequence,
801:        fallbackIndex,
802:        startedAt:      attemptStartedAt,
803:        queuedAt,
804:        label:          `${provider}/${mappedModel}`,
805:        provider,
806:        model:          mappedModel,
807:        sourceType:     ctx.sourceType,
808:        sourceId:       ctx.sourceId ?? null,
809:        featureTag:     ctx.featureTag ?? 'unknown',
810:        organisationId: ctx.organisationId,
811:        subaccountId:   ctx.subaccountId ?? null,
812:        runId:          ctx.runId ?? null,
813:        executionId:    ctx.executionId ?? null,
814:        ieeRunId:       ctx.ieeRunId ?? null,
815:        callSite:       ctx.callSite ?? 'app',
816:        timeoutMs:      PROVIDER_CALL_TIMEOUT_MS,
817:      });
818:      currentRuntimeKey = attemptRuntimeKey;
819:      // Deferred-items brief §7 — capture the payload snapshot so the
820:      // admin live-row drawer can render prompt/system/tools. LRU-bounded
821:      // in-memory store (see llmInflightPayloadStore.ts), cleared on
822:      // registry.remove() below. Snapshot is by-reference in-memory only;
823:      // the store never forwards to the socket or DB.
824:      llmInflightPayloadStore.set(attemptRuntimeKey, {
825:        messages:    params.messages,
826:        system:      params.system,
827:        tools:       params.tools,
828:        maxTokens:   params.maxTokens,
829:        temperature: params.temperature,
830:      });
831:
832:      // TODO(live-agent-execution-log): emit llm.requested + llm.completed
833:      // critical events and write the agent_run_llm_payloads row inside the
834:      // terminal ledger transaction. Scaffolding lives in
835:      // server/services/agentRunPayloadWriter.ts + agentExecutionEventService.
836:      // Wiring here needs the provisional `started` ledger row's id which
837:      // is currently local to the upsert block below — either thread the id
838:      // up, or move the emission to the same transaction that writes the
839:      // terminal row. When wiring, populate agent_run_llm_payloads.run_id
840:      // from ctx.runId (spec §5.7 + post-review hardening — denormalised
841:      // FK closes the "payload not run-scoped" finding). Spec:
842:      // tasks/live-agent-execution-log-spec.md §4.5, §5.3.
843:
844:      try {
845:        providerResponse = await callWithTimeout(
846:          `${provider}/${mappedModel}`,
847:          PROVIDER_CALL_TIMEOUT_MS,
848:          params.abortSignal,
849:          async (signal) => {
850:            // Deferred-items brief §5 — opt into streaming when the caller
851:            // requests it AND the adapter implements `stream()`. Fall
852:            // through to `call()` otherwise. The streaming path emits
853:            // throttled progress events to the in-flight registry as
854:            // tokens arrive; the return shape is identical so the ledger
855:            // write path is unchanged.
856:            if (params.stream && typeof providerAdapter.stream === 'function') {
857:              const iterable = providerAdapter.stream({
858:                model:       mappedModel,
859:                messages:    params.messages,
860:                system:      params.system,
861:                tools:       params.tools,
862:                maxTokens:   params.maxTokens,
863:                temperature: params.temperature,
864:                signal,
865:              });
866:              // pr-review finding #3 (2026-04-21): if the for-await loop
867:              // exits via exception, `iterable.done` is left as an
868:              // unobserved Promise and Node.js emits
869:              // UnhandledPromiseRejection. Attach a no-op catch FIRST so
870:              // the handler is installed before any throw site, then
871:              // await it normally at the end. `await iterable.done`
872:              // re-observes the same Promise; a no-op handler alongside
873:              // the normal await is the standard node idiom for
874:              // "observe a Promise twice without double-reporting".
875:              iterable.done.catch(() => { /* intentional no-op — propagated via for-await */ });
876:              let tokensSoFar = 0;
877:              for await (const chunk of iterable) {
878:                if (typeof chunk.tokensSoFar === 'number') {
879:                  tokensSoFar = chunk.tokensSoFar;
880:                } else if (chunk.deltaText) {
881:                  // Rough token count — 1 per ~4 chars, same heuristic as
882:                  // TOKEN_INPUT_RATIO math. Adapters that surface the
883:                  // accurate tokensSoFar override this estimate.
884:                  tokensSoFar += Math.max(1, Math.round(chunk.deltaText.length / 4));
885:                }
886:                inflightRegistry.emitProgress({
887:                  runtimeKey:     attemptRuntimeKey,
888:                  idempotencyKey,
889:                  tokensSoFar,
890:                });
891:              }
892:              return await iterable.done;
893:            }
894:            return providerAdapter.call({
895:              model:       mappedModel,
896:              messages:    params.messages,
897:              system:      params.system,
898:              tools:       params.tools,
899:              maxTokens:   params.maxTokens,
900:              temperature: params.temperature,
901:              signal,
902:            });
903:          },
904:        );
905:
906:        // Rev §6 — post-process hook. Runs the caller's schema check with
907:        // the raw content. If it throws ParseFailureError, treat like a
908:        // retryable provider error so the fallback loop can try again.
909:        if (params.postProcess) {
910:          try {
911:            await params.postProcess(providerResponse.content);
912:          } catch (postErr) {
913:            if (isParseFailureError(postErr)) {
914:              // Treat parse failure as a retryable error — the fallback loop
915:              // will retry up to PROVIDER_MAX_RETRIES, then the outer catch
916:              // writes the ledger row with status='parse_failure' and the
917:              // excerpt from the final attempt.
918:              providerResponse = null;
919:              throw postErr;
920:            }
921:            throw postErr;
922:          }
923:        }
924:
925:        // Success — record actual provider/model used
926:        actualProvider = provider;
927:        actualModel = mappedModel;
928:        attemptNumber = attempt;
929:        fallbackAttempts.push({ provider, model: mappedModel, success: true });
930:
931:        if (provider !== effectiveProvider || mappedModel !== effectiveModel) {
932:          console.info('[llmRouter] provider_fallback_used', {
933:            requestedProvider: effectiveProvider, requestedModel: effectiveModel,
934:            actualProvider: provider, actualModel: mappedModel,
935:            attemptNumber,
936:            organisationId: ctx.organisationId, runId: ctx.runId,
937:          });
938:        }
939:
940:        break providerLoop;
941:      } catch (err: unknown) {
942:        lastError = err;
943:        fallbackAttempts.push({ provider, model: mappedModel, error: (err as Error).message });
944:
945:        // Non-retryable errors break out to the ledger-write-on-failure path
946:        // below so every terminal attempt produces a ledger row — without
947:        // this, PROVIDER_TIMEOUT / PROVIDER_NOT_CONFIGURED / auth errors
948:        // would skip the ledger entirely and become invisible to the P&L
949:        // surface. The shared failure path at the bottom of this function
950:        // calls releaseReservation() + writes the row + rethrows lastError.
951:        if (isNonRetryableError(err)) {
952:          // Keep `currentRuntimeKey` — the terminal-failure ledger-write
953:          // path below will remove the entry once `ledgerRowId` is known.
954:          break providerLoop;
955:        }
956:
957:        createEvent('llm.router.fallback', {
958:          failedProvider: provider,
959:          failedModel: mappedModel,
960:          error: String(err).slice(0, 200),
961:          attemptIndex: attempt,
962:        });
963:
964:        // Retryable error — remove this attempt's entry from the registry
965:        // before the backoff sleep / next attempt. The next attempt's
966:        // runtimeKey will be distinct (new startedAt) so the pre-add
967:        // invariant above is honoured. Capture the attempt's identity in
968:        // `lastRemovedAttempt` so the failure path can re-emit a
969:        // ledger-linked removal event if all attempts exhaust without
970:        // entering the `currentRuntimeKey != null` path below.
971:        if (currentRuntimeKey) {
972:          inflightRegistry.remove({
973:            runtimeKey:      currentRuntimeKey,
974:            terminalStatus:  'error',
975:            completedAt:     new Date().toISOString(),
976:            ledgerRowId:     null,
977:            ledgerCommittedAt: null,
978:            sweepReason:     null,
979:            evictionContext: null,
980:          });
981:          llmInflightPayloadStore.remove(currentRuntimeKey);
982:          lastRemovedAttempt = {
983:            runtimeKey:     currentRuntimeKey,
984:            idempotencyKey,
985:            attempt,
986:            startedAt:      attemptStartedAt,
987:            terminalStatus: 'error',
988:          };
989:          currentRuntimeKey = null;
990:        }
991:
992:        if (attempt <= PROVIDER_MAX_RETRIES) {
993:          const backoff = PROVIDER_BACKOFF_MS[attempt - 1] ?? PROVIDER_BACKOFF_MS[PROVIDER_BACKOFF_MS.length - 1];
994:          console.warn(`[llmRouter] Provider ${provider} attempt ${attempt} failed, retrying in ${backoff}ms`, {
995:            error: (err as Error).message,
996:          });
997:          await new Promise(r => setTimeout(r, backoff));
998:        }
999:      }
1000:    }
1001:
1002:    // All retries exhausted for this provider — enter cooldown and try next
1003:    if (!providerResponse) {
1004:      providerCooldowns.set(provider, Date.now() + PROVIDER_COOLDOWN_MS);
1005:      console.warn(`[llmRouter] Provider ${provider} exhausted — entering ${PROVIDER_COOLDOWN_MS}ms cooldown`);
1006:    }
1007:  }
1008:
1009:  if (!providerResponse) {
1010:    const e = lastError as { message?: string } | null | undefined;
1011:
1012:    // Rev §6 / April 2026 timeout hardening — single source of truth for
1013:    // error → ledger-status classification lives in llmRouterErrorMappingPure.
1014:    // Every failure mode (parse_failure, client_disconnected, aborted_by_caller,
1015:    // provider_unavailable, provider_not_configured, timeout, generic error)
1016:    // produces a ledger row here — no skip paths.
1017:    const classification   = classifyRouterError(lastError);
1018:    callStatus             = classification.status;
1019:    const abortReasonValue = classification.abortReason;
1020:    const parseFailureExcerpt = classification.parseFailureExcerpt;
1021:
1022:    callError = (e?.message ?? 'All providers failed') + (lastError instanceof Error && lastError.message.includes('timed out') ? ' (timeout)' : '');
1023:
1024:    // Release reservation — no cost incurred (tolerates null for system/analyzer)
1025:    await budgetService.releaseReservation(reservationId);
1026:
1027:    const providerLatencyMs = Date.now() - providerStart;
1028:    const routerOverheadMs  = Date.now() - routerStart - providerLatencyMs;
1029:
1030:    console.error('[llmRouter] All providers failed', {
1031:      idempotencyKey, organisationId: ctx.organisationId, runId: ctx.runId,
1032:      provider: effectiveProvider, model: effectiveModel, status: callStatus, error: callError,
1033:    });
1034:
1035:    const hasFallbackFailures = fallbackAttempts.some(a => a.error);
1036:
1037:    // Phase C breaker is NOT called on the failure path — failure rows record
1038:    // costWithMarginCents=0 and do not contribute to per-run spend. If partial-
1039:    // cost-on-failure is ever introduced, the breaker would need wiring here too.
1040:    // Deferred-items brief §1 — the provisional `'started'` row written
1041:    // at §7a above MUST be overwritten with the terminal failure status
1042:    // here, otherwise a crashed/failed call leaves a `'started'` ghost
1043:    // blocking all retries for this idempotencyKey until the sweep
1044:    // reaps it 660s later. `onConflictDoUpdate` with the same
1045:    // "never downgrade a success" guard as the success path keeps the
1046:    // idempotency semantics intact: a retry that somehow lands here
1047:    // after a success (shouldn't happen but defensive) will no-op.
1048:    const failureInsertedRows = await db
1049:      .insert(llmRequests)
1050:      .values({
1051:        idempotencyKey,
1052:        organisationId:      ctx.organisationId,
1053:        subaccountId:        ctx.subaccountId,
1054:        userId:              ctx.userId,
1055:        sourceType:          ctx.sourceType,
1056:        runId:               ctx.runId,
1057:        executionId:         ctx.executionId,
1058:        ieeRunId:            ctx.ieeRunId,        // §11.7.1
1059:        sourceId:            ctx.sourceId,        // rev §6
1060:        featureTag:          ctx.featureTag ?? 'unknown',  // rev §6
1061:        callSite:            ctx.callSite ?? 'app',
1062:        agentName:           ctx.agentName,
1063:        taskType:            ctx.taskType,
1064:        executionPhase:      ctx.executionPhase,  // nullable for system/analyzer
1065:        capabilityTier:      routingTier,
1066:        wasDowngraded,
1067:        routingReason,
1068:        provider:            effectiveProvider,
1069:        model:               effectiveModel,
1070:        tokensIn:            0,
1071:        tokensOut:           0,
1072:        costRaw:             '0',
1073:        costWithMargin:      '0',
1074:        costWithMarginCents: 0,
1075:        marginMultiplier:    String(margin.multiplier),
1076:        fixedFeeCents:       margin.fixedFeeCents,
1077:        requestPayloadHash,
1078:        providerLatencyMs,
1079:        routerOverheadMs,
1080:        status:              callStatus,
1081:        errorMessage:        callError,
1082:        attemptNumber,
1083:        parseFailureRawExcerpt: parseFailureExcerpt,  // rev §6
1084:        abortReason:         abortReasonValue,       // rev §6
1085:        requestedProvider:   effectiveProvider,
1086:        requestedModel:      effectiveModel,
1087:        fallbackChain:       hasFallbackFailures ? JSON.stringify(fallbackAttempts) : null,
1088:        wasEscalated:        ctx.wasEscalated ?? false,
1089:        escalationReason:    ctx.escalationReason,
1090:        billingMonth,
1091:        billingDay,
1092:      })
1093:      .onConflictDoUpdate({
1094:        target: [llmRequests.idempotencyKey],
1095:        set: {
1096:          status:                 callStatus,
1097:          errorMessage:           callError,
1098:          providerLatencyMs,
1099:          routerOverheadMs,
1100:          attemptNumber,
1101:          parseFailureRawExcerpt: parseFailureExcerpt,
1102:          abortReason:            abortReasonValue,
1103:          fallbackChain:          hasFallbackFailures ? JSON.stringify(fallbackAttempts) : null,
1104:          capabilityTier:         routingTier,
1105:          wasDowngraded,
1106:          routingReason,
1107:          // pr-review finding #4 (2026-04-21): mirror the success set's
1108:          // margin-fields policy so a future move of pricingService.getMargin
1109:          // inside the retry loop can't silently leave stale provisional
1110:          // defaults on the terminal failure row.
1111:          marginMultiplier:       String(margin.multiplier),
1112:          fixedFeeCents:          margin.fixedFeeCents,
1113:        },
1114:        // Reviewer follow-up (2026-04-21): tighten the transition guard from
1115:        // `!= 'success'` to `= 'started'`. The idempotency-check transaction
1116:        // above always leaves the row in 'started' state before this path
1117:        // runs — whether it's a fresh call (INSERT 'started') or a retry
1118:        // after a prior error (onConflictDoUpdate 'started' with fresh
1119:        // createdAt). A mismatch at this point means either (a) the sweep
1120:        // fired and claimed the row as provisional_row_expired, or (b) a
1121:        // second concurrent attempt already terminalised it. In either
1122:        // case the guard preserves the earlier terminal signal; we log
1123:        // the ghost so an operator can reconcile rather than silently
1124:        // losing the audit trail.
1125:        where: sql`${llmRequests.status} = 'started'`,
1126:      })
1127:      .returning({ id: llmRequests.id });
1128:
1129:    if (failureInsertedRows.length === 0) {
1130:      logger.warn('llm_router.failure_upsert_ghost', {
1131:        idempotencyKey,
1132:        callStatus,
1133:        note: 'existing row was not in started state — terminal failure audit discarded (earlier sweep or race)',
1134:      });
1135:    }
1136:
1137:    // Emit the terminal in-flight removal with ledger reconciliation. The
1138:    // caller's UI uses `ledgerRowId` + `ledgerCommittedAt` to link the live
1139:    // row to the ledger detail drawer (spec §5).
1140:    //
1141:    // Two branches:
1142:    //   (a) `currentRuntimeKey` is set — the last attempt was a non-
1143:    //       retryable break (PROVIDER_TIMEOUT, CLIENT_DISCONNECTED,
1144:    //       PROVIDER_NOT_CONFIGURED, auth). The entry is still alive in
1145:    //       the registry; remove it with the now-known ledger row id.
1146:    //   (b) `currentRuntimeKey` is null but `lastRemovedAttempt` is set —
1147:    //       every attempt was a retryable error, and each inner catch
1148:    //       already removed its own entry with `ledgerRowId: null`. The
1149:    //       ledger row has now been written, so we re-emit a ledger-
1150:    //       linked removal for the last attempt's runtimeKey via
1151:    //       `updateLedgerLink`. The client merges the populated
1152:    //       ledgerRowId over the earlier null in `recentlyLanded`, so
1153:    //       the [ledger] button appears on the "Recently landed" row.
1154:    const ledgerRowId = failureInsertedRows[0]?.id ?? null;
1155:    const ledgerCommittedAtISO = ledgerRowId ? new Date().toISOString() : null;
1156:    if (currentRuntimeKey) {
1157:      inflightRegistry.remove({
1158:        runtimeKey:        currentRuntimeKey,
1159:        terminalStatus:    callStatus as
1160:          | 'error' | 'timeout' | 'aborted_by_caller' | 'client_disconnected'
1161:          | 'parse_failure' | 'provider_unavailable' | 'provider_not_configured',
1162:        completedAt:       new Date().toISOString(),
1163:        ledgerRowId,
1164:        ledgerCommittedAt: ledgerCommittedAtISO,
1165:        sweepReason:       null,
1166:        evictionContext:   null,
1167:      });
1168:      llmInflightPayloadStore.remove(currentRuntimeKey);
1169:      currentRuntimeKey = null;
1170:    } else if (lastRemovedAttempt && ledgerRowId && ledgerCommittedAtISO) {
1171:      inflightRegistry.updateLedgerLink({
1172:        runtimeKey:        lastRemovedAttempt.runtimeKey,
1173:        idempotencyKey:    lastRemovedAttempt.idempotencyKey,
1174:        attempt:           lastRemovedAttempt.attempt,
1175:        terminalStatus:    lastRemovedAttempt.terminalStatus,
1176:        completedAt:       new Date().toISOString(),
1177:        durationMs:        Math.max(
1178:          0,
1179:          Date.now() - Date.parse(lastRemovedAttempt.startedAt),
1180:        ),
1181:        ledgerRowId,
1182:        ledgerCommittedAt: ledgerCommittedAtISO,
1183:      });
1184:    }
1185:
1186:    throw lastError ?? new Error('All providers exhausted');
1187:  }
1188:
1189:  const providerLatencyMs = Date.now() - providerStart;
1190:
1191:  // ── 9. Calculate actual cost ─────────────────────────────────────────────
1192:  //
1193:  // Rev §6 — sourceType threaded through so pricingService's resolveMargin
1194:  // can collapse margin to 1.0× for sourceType ∈ {'system','analyzer'}.
1195:  // Downstream effect: costWithMargin === costRaw for overhead rows, so the
1196:  // System P&L page's net-profit math stays honest.
1197:  const costResult = await pricingService.calculateCost(
1198:    actualProvider,
1199:    actualModel,
1200:    providerResponse.tokensIn,
1201:    providerResponse.tokensOut,
1202:    ctx.organisationId,
1203:    providerResponse.cachedPromptTokens ?? 0,
1204:    ctx.sourceType,
1205:  );
1206:
1207:  // ── 10. Compute response payload hash ───────────────────────────────────
1208:  const responsePayloadHash = createHash('sha256')
1209:    .update(JSON.stringify(providerResponse.content))
1210:    .digest('hex');
1211:
1212:  const routerOverheadMs = Date.now() - routerStart - providerLatencyMs;
1213:
1214:  const usedFallback = actualProvider !== effectiveProvider || actualModel !== effectiveModel;
1215:
1216:  // ── 11. Structured log — paper trail before DB write ────────────────────
1217:  console.info('[llmRouter] request_completed', {
1218:    idempotencyKey,
1219:    organisationId:    ctx.organisationId,
1220:    subaccountId:      ctx.subaccountId,
1221:    runId:             ctx.runId,
1222:    provider:          actualProvider,
1223:    model:             actualModel,
1224:    executionPhase:    ctx.executionPhase,
1225:    tier:              routingTier,
1226:    routingReason,
1227:    wasDowngraded,
1228:    cachedPromptTokens: providerResponse.cachedPromptTokens ?? 0,
1229:    ...(usedFallback ? { requestedProvider: effectiveProvider, requestedModel: effectiveModel } : {}),
1230:    providerRequestId: providerResponse.providerRequestId,
1231:    tokensIn:          providerResponse.tokensIn,
1232:    tokensOut:         providerResponse.tokensOut,
1233:    costRaw:           costResult.costRaw,
1234:    costWithMargin:    costResult.costWithMargin,
1235:    costWithMarginCents: costResult.costWithMarginCents,
1236:    requestPayloadHash,
1237:    responsePayloadHash,
1238:    status:            callStatus,
1239:    attemptNumber,
1240:    providerLatencyMs,
1241:    routerOverheadMs,
1242:  });
1243:
1244:  // ── 12. Write ledger — upsert so a successful retry overwrites a prior error row ──
1245:  const hasFallbackFailures = fallbackAttempts.some(a => a.error);
1246:
1247:  const successInsertedRows = await db
1248:    .insert(llmRequests)
1249:    .values({
1250:      idempotencyKey,
1251:      organisationId:      ctx.organisationId,
1252:      subaccountId:        ctx.subaccountId,
1253:      userId:              ctx.userId,
1254:      sourceType:          ctx.sourceType,
1255:      runId:               ctx.runId,
1256:      executionId:         ctx.executionId,
1257:      ieeRunId:            ctx.ieeRunId,        // §11.7.1
1258:      sourceId:            ctx.sourceId,        // rev §6
1259:      featureTag:          ctx.featureTag ?? 'unknown',  // rev §6
1260:      callSite:            ctx.callSite ?? 'app',
1261:      agentName:           ctx.agentName,
1262:      taskType:            ctx.taskType,
1263:      executionPhase:      ctx.executionPhase,  // nullable for system/analyzer
1264:      capabilityTier:      routingTier,
1265:      wasDowngraded,
1266:      routingReason,
1267:      cachedPromptTokens:  providerResponse.cachedPromptTokens ?? 0,
1268:      provider:            actualProvider,
1269:      model:               actualModel,
1270:      providerRequestId:   providerResponse.providerRequestId,
1271:      tokensIn:            providerResponse.tokensIn,
1272:      tokensOut:           providerResponse.tokensOut,
1273:      providerTokensIn:    providerResponse.tokensIn,
1274:      providerTokensOut:   providerResponse.tokensOut,
1275:      costRaw:             String(costResult.costRaw),
1276:      costWithMargin:      String(costResult.costWithMargin),
1277:      costWithMarginCents: costResult.costWithMarginCents,
1278:      marginMultiplier:    String(costResult.marginMultiplier),
1279:      fixedFeeCents:       costResult.fixedFeeCents,
1280:      requestPayloadHash,
1281:      responsePayloadHash,
1282:      providerLatencyMs,
1283:      routerOverheadMs,
1284:      status:              callStatus,
1285:      attemptNumber,
1286:      requestedProvider:   effectiveProvider,
1287:      requestedModel:      effectiveModel,
1288:      fallbackChain:       hasFallbackFailures ? JSON.stringify(fallbackAttempts) : null,
1289:      wasEscalated:        ctx.wasEscalated ?? false,
1290:      escalationReason:    ctx.escalationReason,
1291:      billingMonth,
1292:      billingDay,
1293:    })
1294:    .onConflictDoUpdate({
1295:      target: [llmRequests.idempotencyKey],
1296:      // Only overwrite if the existing row is an error/provisional state —
1297:      // never downgrade success. Deferred-items brief §1: when a provisional
1298:      // `'started'` row exists, the SET clause must fully replace it with
1299:      // the terminal success payload — including provider/model (which may
1300:      // have changed via fallback), capability tier, margin, and cached-
1301:      // prompt tokens. Missing fields leave provisional-row defaults in
1302:      // place and skew downstream cost rollups.
1303:      set: {
1304:        provider:            actualProvider,
1305:        model:               actualModel,
1306:        providerRequestId:   providerResponse.providerRequestId,
1307:        tokensIn:            providerResponse.tokensIn,
1308:        tokensOut:           providerResponse.tokensOut,
1309:        providerTokensIn:    providerResponse.tokensIn,
1310:        providerTokensOut:   providerResponse.tokensOut,
1311:        cachedPromptTokens:  providerResponse.cachedPromptTokens ?? 0,
1312:        costRaw:             String(costResult.costRaw),
1313:        costWithMargin:      String(costResult.costWithMargin),
1314:        costWithMarginCents: costResult.costWithMarginCents,
1315:        marginMultiplier:    String(costResult.marginMultiplier),
1316:        fixedFeeCents:       costResult.fixedFeeCents,
1317:        responsePayloadHash,
1318:        providerLatencyMs,
1319:        routerOverheadMs,
1320:        status:              callStatus,
1321:        errorMessage:        null,
1322:        attemptNumber,
1323:        capabilityTier:      routingTier,
1324:        wasDowngraded,
1325:        routingReason,
1326:        fallbackChain:       hasFallbackFailures ? JSON.stringify(fallbackAttempts) : null,
1327:      },
1328:      // Reviewer follow-up (2026-04-21): tighten from `!= 'success'` to
1329:      // `= 'started'`. The idempotency-check transaction always leaves
1330:      // the row in 'started' before this path runs. A mismatch here means
1331:      // another terminal transition has already happened (sweep fired and
1332:      // claimed as `provisional_row_expired`, or a prior retry
1333:      // terminalised). Tightening preserves the earlier terminal signal
1334:      // — the sweep's "call went long enough that something was wrong"
1335:      // signal is operationally more valuable than a late-arriving
1336:      // success that pretends everything was fine. Ghost arrivals are
1337:      // logged below so operators can reconcile.
1338:      where: sql`${llmRequests.status} = 'started'`,
1339:    })
1340:    .returning({ id: llmRequests.id });
1341:
1342:  const successLedgerRowId = successInsertedRows[0]?.id ?? null;
1343:
1344:  if (successInsertedRows.length === 0) {
1345:    // Mismatch path — either (a) an identical success already exists
1346:    // (idempotency replay — the prior success row has status='success'
1347:    // which our tightened guard correctly refuses to re-overwrite), or
1348:    // (b) the sweep/sibling raced and terminalised with a non-success
1349:    // status. The breaker skip path below already tolerates a null
1350:    // successLedgerRowId by treating it as idempotency replay; this
1351:    // log surfaces the case so operators can spot the "true success
1352:    // was discarded by the sweep" variant from the ledger audit.
1353:    logger.warn('llm_router.success_upsert_ghost', {
1354:      idempotencyKey,
1355:      note: 'terminal success could not transition from started (already success, or sweep/sibling claimed it as terminal-error)',
1356:    });
1357:  }
1358:
1359:  // ── 12a. Hermes Tier 1 Phase C — runaway-loop cost breaker ───────────────
1360:  //
1361:  // Call the direct-ledger breaker AFTER the ledger row is durably written
1362:  // and BEFORE the in-flight registry is cleaned up. Ordering rationale
1363:  // pinned in tasks/hermes-audit-tier-1-spec.md §7.3 / §7.4 / §7.4.1:
1364:  //
1365:  //   1. Ledger write first → cost attribution is intact regardless of
1366:  //      whether the breaker trips. The money was already spent with the
1367:  //      provider; recording it is non-negotiable.
1368:  //   2. Direct-ledger read (not cost_aggregates) → cost_aggregates is
1369:  //      updated asynchronously by `routerJobService.enqueueAggregateUpdate`
1370:  //      below, so a rollup-based read would miss this call's cost and
1371:  //      inflate worst-case overshoot by the aggregation-interval's worth
1372:  //      of concurrent traffic.
1373:  //   3. `insertedLedgerRowId` threaded through as REQUIRED parameter →
1374:  //      the helper performs a row-visibility check and fails closed on
1375:  //      null or not-visible. Structural guarantee against a future
1376:  //      refactor that swaps the call above the ledger insert.
1377:  //   4. Skip entirely when runId cannot be resolved (sourceType ∈
1378:  //      {'system','analyzer'} have no run context; IEE runs map via
1379:  //      `resolveRunIdFromIee` below). See §7.5 / §7.6.
1380:  //   5. Fail-open on infra errors (non-'cost_limit_exceeded' throws) →
1381:  //      the breaker is secondary protection; a DB hiccup in the breaker's
1382:  //      own read must not take down the LLM path, which is the primary
1383:  //      business function. `costBreaker.infra_failure` is the signal ops
1384:  //      uses to notice.
1385:  //
1386:  // If the breaker throws `cost_limit_exceeded`, the in-flight registry
1387:  // entry is orphaned until the sweep runs — acceptable per §7.3.2 because
1388:  // the sweep is the existing safety net for orphaned entries and the
1389:  // three-branch cleanup pattern above predates Phase C.
1390:  const breakerRunId = ctx.runId ?? (await resolveRunIdFromIee(ctx.ieeRunId));
1391:  if (breakerRunId) {
1392:    if (!successLedgerRowId) {
1393:      // Upsert hit the `where status = 'started'` guard — existing row is
1394:      // not in 'started' state. Either an idempotency replay against a
1395:      // prior success, or the sweep / sibling claimed the row with a
1396:      // terminal-error status (see ghost log above). Skip the breaker
1397:      // either way — the first insert owns the cost attribution.
1398:      console.debug('[llmRouter] costBreaker.skip_terminal_preempted', { correlationId: idempotencyKey });
1399:    } else {
1400:      try {
1401:        const { assertWithinRunBudgetFromLedger } = await import('../lib/runCostBreaker.js');
1402:        await assertWithinRunBudgetFromLedger({
1403:          runId:               breakerRunId,
1404:          insertedLedgerRowId: successLedgerRowId,
1405:          subaccountAgentId:   ctx.subaccountAgentId ?? null,
1406:          organisationId:      ctx.organisationId,
1407:          // The router ctx does not carry a distinct correlationId; the LLM
1408:          // idempotencyKey is the stable per-call identifier we thread
1409:          // through downstream logs and the breaker's trip payload.
1410:          correlationId:       idempotencyKey,
1411:        });
1412:        console.debug('[llmRouter] costBreaker.checked', {
1413:          runId:         breakerRunId,
1414:          correlationId: idempotencyKey,
1415:        });
1416:      } catch (err) {
1417:        const isExpectedBreakerTrip =
1418:          err instanceof FailureError &&
1419:          err.failure.failureReason === 'internal_error' &&
1420:          err.failure.failureDetail === 'cost_limit_exceeded';
1421:        if (isExpectedBreakerTrip) {
1422:          // Commit the reservation and enqueue the aggregate update before
1423:          // rethrowing — without these calls the over-budget call's cost stays
1424:          // locked in an active reservation and cost_aggregates never receives
1425:          // the row, so RunCostPanel and aggregate-backed readers permanently
1426:          // undercount the triggering call's spend. Both calls are best-effort:
1427:          // failures here must not mask the cost_limit_exceeded error.
1428:          budgetService.commitReservation(reservationId, costResult.costWithMarginCents).catch((e) => {
1429:            console.error('[llmRouter] costBreaker.commit_reservation_failed', {
1430:              runId: breakerRunId, correlationId: idempotencyKey,
1431:              error: e instanceof Error ? e.message : String(e),
1432:            });
1433:          });
1434:          enqueueAggregateUpdate(idempotencyKey).catch((e) => {
1435:            console.error('[llmRouter] costBreaker.enqueue_aggregate_failed', {
1436:              runId: breakerRunId, correlationId: idempotencyKey,
1437:              error: e instanceof Error ? e.message : String(e),
1438:            });
1439:          });
1440:          throw err;
1441:        }
1442:        console.error('[llmRouter] costBreaker.infra_failure', {
1443:          runId:         breakerRunId,
1444:          correlationId: idempotencyKey,
1445:          error:         err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err),
1446:        });
1447:      }
1448:    }
1449:  }
1450:
1451:  // ── 12b. Remove the in-flight registry entry for the successful attempt ──
1452:  // Emitted AFTER the ledger upsert so `ledgerRowId` + `ledgerCommittedAt`
1453:  // are populated on the removal payload (spec §5). When the upsert hits
1454:  // the `where: status != 'success'` guard on an already-success row,
1455:  // `.returning()` comes back empty — we fall back to `null` and the UI
1456:  // retries via idempotencyKey.
1457:  if (currentRuntimeKey) {
1458:    inflightRegistry.remove({
1459:      runtimeKey:        currentRuntimeKey,
1460:      terminalStatus:    'success',
1461:      completedAt:       new Date().toISOString(),
1462:      ledgerRowId:       successLedgerRowId,
1463:      ledgerCommittedAt: successLedgerRowId ? new Date().toISOString() : null,
1464:      sweepReason:       null,
1465:      evictionContext:   null,
1466:    });
1467:    llmInflightPayloadStore.remove(currentRuntimeKey);
1468:    currentRuntimeKey = null;
1469:  }
1470:
1471:  // ── 13. Emit Langfuse generation span (dual-write — does not replace ledger) ──
1472:  createGeneration('llm.router.call', {
1473:    model: actualModel,
1474:    input: params.messages,
1475:    output: providerResponse.content,
1476:    modelParameters: params.maxTokens ? { maxTokens: params.maxTokens } : undefined,
1477:    usage: {
1478:      input: providerResponse.tokensIn,
1479:      output: providerResponse.tokensOut,
1480:    },
1481:    metadata: {
1482:      provider: actualProvider,
1483:      agentName: ctx.agentName,
1484:      taskType: ctx.taskType,
1485:      executionPhase: ctx.executionPhase,
1486:      routingTier,
1487:      wasDowngraded,
1488:      routingReason,
1489:      wasEscalated: ctx.wasEscalated ?? false,
1490:      escalationReason: ctx.escalationReason ?? null,
1491:      attemptNumber,
1492:      criticalPath: true,
1493:    },
1494:  });
1495:
1496:  // ── 14. Commit reservation with actual cost (releases delta) ─────────────
1497:  // commitReservation tolerates null (system/analyzer paths never reserve).
1498:  await budgetService.commitReservation(reservationId, costResult.costWithMarginCents);
1499:
1500:  // ── 15. Enqueue aggregate update (async — do not await) ──────────────────
1501:  enqueueAggregateUpdate(idempotencyKey).catch((err) => {
1502:    console.error('[llmRouter] Failed to enqueue aggregate update', err);
1503:  });
1504:
1505:  // ── 16. Attach routing metadata for caller visibility ───────────────────
1506:  providerResponse.routing = {
1507:    tier: routingTier,
1508:    wasDowngraded,
1509:    reason: routingReason,
1510:  };
1511:
1512:  return providerResponse;
1513:}
1514:
1515:// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
1516:// Enqueue aggregate update via pg-boss (or in-memory fallback)
1517:// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
1518:
1519:async function enqueueAggregateUpdate(idempotencyKey: string): Promise<void> {
1520:  try {
1521:    const { routerJobService } = await import('./routerJobService.js');
1522:    await routerJobService.enqueueAggregateUpdate(idempotencyKey);
1523:  } catch {
1524:    // Fallback: run synchronously if queue service unavailable
1525:    const [request] = await db
1526:      .select()
1527:      .from(llmRequests)
1528:      .where(eq(llmRequests.idempotencyKey, idempotencyKey))
1529:      .limit(1);
1530:
1531:    if (request) {
1532:      const { costAggregateService } = await import('./costAggregateService.js');
1533:      await costAggregateService.upsertAggregates(request);
1534:    }
1535:  }
1536:}

tasks\review-logs\_spec-review-crm-query-planner-iter2-codex-output.txt:14401:9. The new `crm.query` action entry still does not match the real `ACTION_REGISTRY` schema. This is concrete contract drift against an existing source of truth.

The planner parses that content into `DraftQueryPlan`. `postProcess` runs inside the router for ledger attribution; the explicit re-parse after the call gives the planner the typed object for downstream use — both use the same `DraftQueryPlanSchema`, so there is one authority for the response shape.
786:function resolvePlannerTier(orgId: string, escalate: boolean): ModelTier {
846:**Stage contract:** given a `DraftQueryPlan` + `SchemaContext` + `CanonicalQueryRegistry`, return a validated `QueryPlan` or `ValidationError`.
881:throw new ValidationError({
888:The caller (`crmQueryPlannerService`) catches `ValidationError` and emits `BriefErrorResult { errorCode: 'ambiguous_intent', message, suggestions }`. **No retry.** No second LLM call. The refinement is the user's next Brief.
907:- One fail case per rule (rule's check fails, `ValidationError` thrown with correct `rejectedRule`)
923:  context: ExecutorContext
941:      throw new MissingPermissionError(cap);
956:`MissingPermissionError` is a small service-layer error thrown by the executor and caught by `crmQueryPlannerService.ts` → emitted as `BriefErrorResult { errorCode: 'missing_permission', message }`.
1136:  context: ExecutorContext
1157:`translateToProviderQuery(plan)` is a pure function in `liveExecutor.ts`. It maps the plan's `filters`, `sort`, `limit`, `projection`, `dateContext` to a `TranslatedGhlRead` object with an `endpoint` discriminant (e.g. `'listContacts'`) plus the parameter object the matching `ghlReadHelpers` function accepts. `TranslatedGhlRead` is declared inside `liveExecutor.ts`; it is the planner's local type and does not touch the adapter surface. The dispatch layer (`dispatchGhlRead`, §13.1) is the single place that knows which helper belongs to which endpoint value.
1179:- Plan translation is deterministic per input — each `plan.primaryEntity` maps to the correct `TranslatedGhlRead.endpoint`
1198:  context: ExecutorContext
1257:  context: NormaliserContext
1304:  context: NormaliserContext
1340:`context.defaultSenderIdentifier` is a new `NormaliserContext` field populated from the caller's permission context (see §16.4) — it's the CRM-connected sender identifier for the subaccount (existing convention in `crm.send_email` dispatch paths). If the subaccount has no connected sender, the card generator skips email-card emission.
1413:  - Stage 3 token counts come from the `ProviderResponse.usage` returned by `llmRouter.routeCall` (the router does NOT return ledger rows — ledger persistence is its internal side-effect; the `usage` object is the caller-visible cost signal). `crmQueryPlannerService` captures the `usage` object from each Stage 3 call (initial parse + optional escalation retry) and feeds it to the calculator.

1398:There is exactly one planner-side cost calculator (`plannerCostPure.ts`) and exactly one source-of-truth field (`QueryPlan.costPreview: BriefCostPreview`, §6.2). codex
The iter-2 fixes mostly landed where expected: the spec now derives `organisationId/userId/runId` from auth instead of the request body, the `crm.query` entry is described in real `ActionDefinition` terms, `withPrincipalContext` is no longer treated like a standalone tx wrapper, and executor-side `requiredCapabilities` are now explicitly enforced. The remaining issues are new or newly exposed by those edits.

1. `llmRouter.routeCall` is still described two different ways, and one of them is wrong against the repo contract. `spec.md:157-159` and `spec.md:1375-1388` still use retired top-level `task` / `model` args, `orgId`, and `systemCallerPolicy: 'strict'`; `spec.md:722-732` is closer, but still assumes the planner can pass tier names like `'haiku'/'sonnet'` straight into `context.model`. The real router only accepts `context.taskType`, `context.organisationId`, optional `context.model`, and `systemCallerPolicy` values `'respect_routing' | 'bypass_routing'` (`server/services/llmRouter.ts:50-90`, `97-120`, `262-345`). In bypass mode it expects a concrete provider/model string, not an abstract tier.

2. The cost contract is still broken against `shared/types/briefResultContract.ts`. `BriefCostPreview` is only `{ predictedCostCents, confidence, basedOn }` in `shared/types/briefResultContract.ts:162-167`, but `spec.md:1398-1417` turns it into a structure with separate predicted/actual slots and even reads `computePlannerCost(...).actual.cents`. That is direct contract drift. It also cascades into `QueryPlan.costPreview` and `DraftQueryPlan` (`spec.md:390`, `394`): as written, the LLM schema would have to emit planner-derived cost data, which contradicts the “single calculator, single source of truth” claim.

3. `runCostBreaker` is wired to the wrong primitive. `spec.md:1392-1417` says `assertWithinRunBudgetFromLedger` runs before Stage 3 and before live dispatch, but the real helper requires an already-inserted `llm_requests` row id and is explicitly the post-ledger sibling used by `llmRouter` (`server/lib/runCostBreaker.ts:203-291`). This also conflicts with `spec.md:1537`, which says human callers may have no `runId`, while `spec.md:1392` says every invocation runs inside one.

4. The permission-sensitive validation contract is still internally inconsistent. Stage 1 is declared as `NormalisedIntent + registry -> QueryPlan|null` (`spec.md:586`), and Stage 4 as `DraftQueryPlan + SchemaContext + CanonicalQueryRegistry -> QueryPlan|ValidationError` (`spec.md:846`), but both `spec.md:640` and Rule 9 at `spec.md:874` require caller-specific permission data. Then `spec.md:692` references “Rule 11” on cache hits even though §11 only defines 9 rules. There still is no single authoritative signature for permission-aware validation.

5. The agent-log event wiring cannot work as written. The spec says raw `planner.*` events are forwarded via `tryEmitAgentEvent` (`spec.md:1453-1469`, `1476-1488`), but the existing agent execution log only accepts the closed `AgentExecutionEventType` union and a required `runId` / known `sourceService` (`shared/types/agentExecutionLog.ts:11-18`, `64-72`, `248-258`; `server/services/agentExecutionEventService.ts:47-52`). `PlannerEvent.runId` is optional in the spec (`spec.md:500-507`), and human callers explicitly may not have one (`spec.md:1537`). If these planner events are meant to land there, the spec must inventory changes to `shared/types/agentExecutionLog.ts` and the append service.

6. The live-executor section still overstates the existing GHL read surface, and §5 misses the file change that would be needed. `spec.md:1153-1157` talks about endpoint dispatch for opportunities, appointments, conversations, tasks, and users, but `server/services/adapters/ghlReadHelpers.ts:147-190` currently only exports `listGhlAutomations`, `listGhlContacts`, `listGhlUsers`, `listGhlFromAddresses`, and `listGhlFromNumbers`. `spec.md:225-253` does not list `server/services/adapters/ghlReadHelpers.ts` as `[existing — extend]`, even though the prose now depends on adding helpers there.

7. The capability source of truth is still missing. The spec now consistently uses `crm.query` plus per-entry capabilities like `canonical.contacts.read` and `clientpulse.health_snapshots.read` (`spec.md:410`, `972-1065`, `1551-1594`, `1763-1788`), but those slugs do not appear anywhere in repo search outside this spec/review log. `spec.md:1120-1124` even proposes validating them against `server/lib/permissions.ts or equivalent`, but no actual equivalent is named. That leaves route gating, rollout, executor gating, and tests without an anchored taxonomy.

8. Stale rate-limiter “release” language survived the iter-2 correction. `spec.md:1173` correctly says the limiter has no `release()`, matching `server/lib/rateLimiter.ts:35-55`, but `spec.md:1662` and `1726` still require acquire/release behavior in P2/test coverage.

9. `readPath: 'canonical'` on `crm.query` is structurally misleading. In the real `ActionDefinition` contract, `readPath` says where the action reads from (`server/config/actionRegistry.ts:109-123`); it is not a generic “read-only” marker. But `spec.md:1575` sets the planner to `'canonical'` while explicitly allowing live and hybrid execution. That will skew the repo’s read-path reporting and gates.

10. “No schema changes” still contradicts the file inventory. `spec.md:250-251` and `729` explicitly extend `server/db/schema/llmRequests.ts` to add `crm_query_planner` to `TASK_TYPES`, but success criterion 11 says `db/schema/` is unchanged (`spec.md:1869`). If the intent is “no DB migration”, that needs to be stated that way.

11. A couple of “existing primitive” claims are still ungrounded. `spec.md:1537` references an existing `requireAgentRunContext()` helper that does not appear in repo search, and `spec.md:1319-1340` introduces `NormaliserContext.defaultSenderIdentifier` as if it follows an existing `crm.send_email` convention, but that identifier is not present elsewhere either. Those should either become explicitly new primitives with file ownership, or the prose should stop treating them as already-available.

12. Minor stale metric language remains: `planner.canonical_hit_rate = canonical_classified / total_queries` at `spec.md:1497`, but the event set only defines `planner.classified`, not `canonical_classified` (`spec.md:1476-1488`).

If you want, I can turn this into an “apply list” grouped by section so the next spec edit pass is mechanical.
